{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 21:30:10","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 13:30:10","title":"Singapore-based Volopay wants to be the “Brex of Southeast Asia”","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024893","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><div id=\"attachment_2024894\" style=\"width: 778px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024894\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2024894\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"768\" height=\"512\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 768px) 100vw, 768px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024894\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/volopay\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"volopay\">Volopay <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> founders Rajith Shaji and Rajesh Raikwar</p></div></p>\n<p>Small- to medium-sized companies that do a lot of international business have to deal with two big headaches: high foreign exchange fees and corporate expense tracking. <a href=\"https://www.volopay.co/\">Volopay</a>, a Singapore-based financial tech startup with offices in Bangalore, wants to help by integrating prepaid multi-currency corporate cards, expense tracking and accounting tools into one free-to-use platform.</p>\n<p>Volopay is currently taking part in Y Combinator and is also part of Antler and Nium’s Bolt, two other accelerator programs. It now has about 40 clients in Singapore, mostly tech startups like Dathena, Tookitaki and Appknox, and plans to launch in Indonesia and Australia within the next six months.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The company was founded last year by chief executive officer Rajith Shaji and chief technology officer Rajesh Raikwar, who met while working at MoneySmart, a financial services comparison platform. Before joining MoneySmart, Shaji also held positions at <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/aax-b20d\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"aax-b20d\">fintech <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> companies like CompareAsiaGroup, MatchMove and BankBazaar.com.</p>\n<p>Shaji spent most of his time working in India, but often traveled to offices abroad. Dealing with corporate expenses after every trip was a &#8220;nightmare,&#8221; Shaji told TechCrunch.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Each time I went back home, I had to make a list of all my expenses on behalf of the company. First of all, it often ran up to a few thousand dollars and I had to put in all these receipts and everything,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>Shaji did not have access to most of the accounting software used by the companies&#8217; accounting departments and communicating with them across different time zones made the process even more cumbersome and time-consuming.</p>\n<p>Volopay addresses those issues by combining prepaid multi-currency corporate cards (available as physical or virtual cards), domestic and international bank transfers, automated payments, and expense and accounting software on one platform. Volopay&#8217;s app lets employees ask for more funds for their prepaid cards from managers, who can approve or reject the request instantly.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg\"><img class=\"alignright wp-image-2024895 size-large\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"453\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg 1600w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=150,100 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=680,453 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=1536,1024 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?resize=50,33 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Shaji said this saves companies money on foreign exchange fees, which are typically about 3% of a transaction on a traditional credit card, and gives them real-time visibility into spending.</p>\n<p>Volopay is free to use and earns money through the interchange fees credit cards charge merchants. Interchange fees also enable Volopay to offer perks like cashback deals.</p>\n<p>Shaji said the company aspires to be the &#8220;Brex of Southeast Asia.&#8221; Like Brex, it offers an alternative to traditional financial services for startups and other small- to mid-sized businesses. But it needs to compete with several companies that also want to solve some of the same problems, like high fees for cross-border banking and corporate expense tracking. For example, Transferwise and Revolut both have operations in Singapore, while Neat and Aspire, based in Hong Kong and Singapore respectively, offer online business accounts.</p>\n<p>Shaji said Volopay&#8217;s integration of multiple services on one platform gives it a competitive edge, adding that a better comparison to his startup is YouTrip, a multi-currency wallet for consumers that is popular in Singapore.</p>\n<p>With accounts linked to a prepaid Mastercard, YouTrip users can make payments in 150 currencies without fees and it also supports in-app foreign currency exchanges. When explaining Volopay to potential clients, Shaji often refers to it as &#8220;YouTrip for companies.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;YouTrip is a well-known brand [in Singapore], everyone knows they can load their money on it and save money on foreign exchange,&#8221; he said. Volopay gives the same functionality to companies, with accounting software added.</p>\n<p>Volopay currently focuses on serving small businesses with 25 or more employees, especially tech startups that are scaling their operations and therefore need to manage increasing numbers of online payments and expenses. Shaji said Volopay has also signed up several marketing agencies, because many work on multiple projects, and therefore have to juggle multiple budgets at once.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=H_z17WAvDGo:M3XyfqR7330:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a Shu","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-team.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn96@2020_1/2020-07-30/1596115814409_bd6104540375ab8d.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Volopay-product-hero-image.jpg?w=680":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn32@2020_2/2020-07-30/1596115828249_0bab0625e5829c77.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn92@2020_6/2020-07-30/1596115814221_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn72@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115829689_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn48@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115828238_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=H_z17WAvDGo:M3XyfqR7330:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn3@2020_1/2020-07-30/1596115830815_439d3412b11b0b0f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=H_z17WAvDGo:M3XyfqR7330:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn60@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115830047_424735f8213f8335.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn92@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115830290_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/H_z17WAvDGo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn64@2020_2/2020-07-30/1596115828115_b57045ea393de1a5.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 21:30:10","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 13:30:10","title":"Buildots raises $16M to bring computer vision to construction management","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024289","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https://buildots.com/\">Buildots</a>, a Tel Aviv and London-based startup that is using computer vision to modernize the construction management industry, today announced that it has raised $16 million in total funding. This includes a $3 million seed round that was previously unreported and a $13 million Series A round, both led by TLV Partners. Other investors include <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.6\">Innogy</span> Ventures, <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.7\">Tidhar</span> Construction Group, <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.8\">Ziv</span> <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.9\">Aviram (</span>co-founder of <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.10\">Mobileye</span> &#38; <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.11\">OrCam)</span>, Magma Ventures head <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.12\">Zvika</span> <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.13\">Limon</span>, serial entrepreneurs Benny <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.14\">Schnaider</span> and  Avigdor <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.15\">Willenz</span>, as well as Tidhar chairman Gil <span id=\"m_9130234700650491450:7xd.16\">Geva.</span></p>\n<p>The idea behind <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/buildots\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"buildots\">Buildots <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> is pretty straightforward. The team is using hardhat-mounted 360-degree cameras to allow project managers at construction sites to get an overview of the state of a project and whether it remains on schedule. The company&#8217;s software creates a digital twin of the construction site, using the architectural plans and schedule as its basis, and then uses computer vision to compare what the plans say to the reality that its tools are seeing. With this, Buildots can immediately detect when there&#8217;s a power outlet missing in a room or whether there&#8217;s a sink that still needs to be installed in a kitchen, for example.</p>\n<p><span id=\"m_-4438620397716549337:7xd.29\"><span class=\"il\">&#8220;Buildots</span></span> have been able to solve a challenge that for many seemed unconquerable, delivering huge potential for changing the way we complete our projects,&#8221; said Tidhar&#8217;s <span id=\"m_-4438620397716549337:7xd.30\">Geva in a statement</span>. &#8220;The combination of an ambitious vision, great team and strong execution abilities quickly led us from being a customer to joining as an investor to take part in their journey.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/1u1hhrMVBvw?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<p>The company was co-founded in 2018 by Roy <span id=\"m_-4438620397716549337:7xd.23\">Danon</span>, <span id=\"m_-4438620397716549337:7xd.24\">Aviv</span> <span id=\"m_-4438620397716549337:7xd.25\">Leibovici</span> and <span id=\"m_-4438620397716549337:7xd.26\">Yakir</span> Sundry. Like so many Israeli startups, the founders met during their time in the Israeli Defense Forces, where they graduated from the <a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Talpiot_program\">Talpiot unit</a>.</p>\n<p>&#8220;At some point, like many of our friends, we had the urge to do something together &#8212; to build a company, to start something from scratch,&#8221; said Danon, the company&#8217;s CEO. &#8220;For us, we like getting our hands dirty. We saw most of our friends going into the most standard industries like cloud and cyber and storage and things that obviously people like us feel more comfortable in, but for some reason we had like a bug that said, &#8216;we want to do something that is a bit harder, that has a bigger impact on the world.&#8217; &#8221;</p>\n<p>So the team started looking into how it could bring technology to traditional industries like agriculture, finance and medicine, but then settled upon construction thanks to a chance meeting with a construction company. For the first six months, the team mostly did research in both Israel and London to understand where it could provide value.</p>\n<p>Danon argues that the construction industry is essentially a manufacturing industry, but with very outdated control and process management systems that still often relies on Excel to track progress.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2024295\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Side-by-side.png\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024295\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2024295\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Side-by-side.png\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"576\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Side-by-side.png 1920w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Side-by-side.png?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Side-by-side.png?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Side-by-side.png?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Side-by-side.png?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Side-by-side.png?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Side-by-side.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024295\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Buildots</p></div></p>\n<p>Construction sites obviously pose their own problems. There&#8217;s often no Wi-Fi, for example, so contractors generally still have to upload their videos manually to Buildots&#8217; servers. They are also three dimensional, so the team had to develop systems to understand on what floor a video was taken, for example, and for large indoor spaces, GPS won&#8217;t work either.</p>\n<p>The teams tells me that before the COVID-19 lockdowns, it was mostly focused on Israel and the U.K., but the pandemic actually accelerated its push into other geographies. It just started work on a large project in Poland and is scheduled to work on another one in Japan next month.</p>\n<p>Because the construction industry is very project-driven, sales often start with getting one project manager on board. That project manager also usually owns the budget for the project, so they can often also sign the check, Danon noted. And once that works out, then the general contractor often wants to talk to the company about a larger enterprise deal.</p>\n<p>As for the funding, the company&#8217;s Series A round came together just before the lockdowns started. The company managed to bring together an interesting mix of investors from both the construction and technology industries.</p>\n<p>Now, the plan is to scale the company, which currently has 35 employees, and figure out even more ways to use the data the service collects and make it useful for its users. &#8220;We have a long journey to turn all the data we have into supporting all the workflows on a construction site,&#8221; said Danon. &#8220;There are so many more things to do and so many more roles to support.&#8221;</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2024296\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/IMG_3377.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024296\" class=\"size-full wp-image-2024296\" 21:30:10","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 13:30:10","title":"Apple’s App Store commission structure called into question in antitrust hearing","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024333","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/apple\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"apple\">Apple <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> CEO Tim Cook defended the company’s App Store commission structure in his sworn testimony before the House Antitrust Subcommittee on Wednesday. He claimed the majority of the apps pay no commission at all, with others paying either 15 or 30 percent, based on the specifics of their particular situation. He said developers were all treated equally and that Apple wouldn&#8217;t raise commissions, because it had to compete for developer interest in its platform as well.</p>\n<p>But the documents shared by the House subcommittee as part of their investigation indicate that exceptions to Apple&#8217;s rules have been made &#8212; notably, with Amazon&#8217;s Prime Video app. In addition, Apple may have never raised commissions, but discussions weren&#8217;t off the table. It had once even considered raising commissions to 40% in particular situations.</p>\n<p>The lawmakers had come to the hearing armed with internal Apple emails and interviews from App Store developers who argued that Apple doesn’t uniformly enforce its rules and plays favorites. But their questioning of Cook over App Store fees, combined with a format that limited execs’ ability to respond at length, initially seemed to reveal little in terms of new information about Apple&#8217;s practices.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>For instance, when asked directly about how the App Store worked, Cook simply restated the store&#8217;s published rules — that is, for app developers who have to pay commissions, they pay only 15 or 30 percent. The current guidelines require 30% for apps selling digital goods or services, with a drop to 15% in year two for subscription apps. The rules also document a carve-out for “reader” apps like audiobook apps, streaming services, news publications, and other competitive products which have the option of forgoing in-app purchases.</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<p>Cook also squeezed in a mention about how the vast majority of App Store apps, 84%, pay nothing to Apple in commissions. It&#8217;s the remaining 16% that pay, he noted.</p>\n<p>And when asked if Apple was the sole gatekeeper as to what gets published on the App Store, Cook agreed that it was — given that the App Store was a “feature of the iPhone, much like the Camera and the chip is.” He clarified that Apple’s control over apps only extended to native software applications, not web apps, but denied Apple treated developers unfairly.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We treat every developer the same. We have open and transparent rules,&#8221; Cook said, in his testimony. &#8220;It&#8217;s a rigorous process, because we care so deeply about privacy and security and quality. We do look at every app before it goes on,” he added.</p>\n<p>But emails in 2016 between Apple SVP Eddy Cue and Amazon CEO Jeff Bezos, shared <a href=\"https://judiciary.house.gov/uploadedfiles/27753.pdf\">here</a> on the House Judiciary Committee&#8217;s website, indicate that Apple, in fact, appears to have negotiated a special deal with Amazon over its Amazon Prime Video app for iOS and Apple TV.  In an email dated Nov. 2016 &#8212; before the <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/12/06/amazon-prime-video-finally-lands-on-apple-tv/\">2017 launch of the Prime Video tvOS app</a> &#8212;  Apple agreed to take only a 15% revenue share for customers that signed up in the app using Apple&#8217;s payment mechanism. (Typically, subscription apps don&#8217;t drop from 30% to 15% until year two.)</p>\n<p>Apple this April confirmed <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/01/in-a-significant-change-apple-customers-can-now-buy-or-rent-titles-directly-in-the-prime-video-app/\"> it had a special program for Prime Video</a> and a small handful of other apps, which were subscription video entertainment providers. The program allowed those companies to rent or sell movies and TV shows to customers using the payment methods the companies already had on file, as well as more deeply integrate with Siri. But Apple hadn&#8217;t said that this special program would include a reduced commission on subscriptions or any other in-app upsells, as these emails confirm were points of discussion.</p>\n<p>This wouldn&#8217;t be the first time Apple saw its commission structure as having some room to flex.</p>\n<p>When Cook was questioned as to whether there was anything that could stop Apple from raising commissions to, say, 50%, the CEO responded that Apple had never increased commissions since day one. He also argued, when asked if anything could stop it from doing so, that competition for developer interest would stop it from raising its cut.</p>\n<p>&#8220;There is a competition for developers, just like there&#8217;s a competition for customers. And so the competition for developers &#8212; they write their apps for Android or Windows or Xbox or Playstation,&#8221; said Cook. &#8220;We have fierce competition on the developer side and the customer side which is essentially &#8212; it&#8217;s so competitive, I would describe it as a street fight for market share in the smartphone business,&#8221; he added.</p>\n<p>But in internal emails from 2011, Apple did discuss raising commissions &#8212; all the way to 40% for the first year of recurring subscriptions. &#8220;I think we may be leaving money on the table if we just asked for about 30% of the first year of sub,&#8221; Cue had written at the time.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\">\n<p dir=\"ltr\" lang=\"en\">Documents from the Hearing on “Online Platforms and Market Power: Examining the Dominance of Amazon, Apple, Facebook and Google&#8221; <a href=\"https://t.co/42o2Ye13jI\">pic.twitter.com/42o2Ye13jI</a></p>\n<p>— House Judiciary Dems (@HouseJudiciary) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/HouseJudiciary/status/1288567281396711426?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 29, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p>Of course, Apple didn&#8217;t go so far as to actually make that change in the years that passed. But these emails indicate there&#8217;s more to Apple&#8217;s thinking &#8212; and its discussions around the commission structure &#8212; than the even playing field Cook testified to.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/tech-antitrust-hearing\"><img src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tech-antitrust-hearing-banner.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=XlpdmL_I7xo:ABONlZk9tJQ:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/XlpdmL_I7xo\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 30 Jul 2020 01:39:21 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tech-antitrust-hearing-banner.jpg","linkMd5":"aa21cb40df6c1685f04cf18a1b6d124e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn84@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596115814639_b509d3f7f12e9f30.webp","author":"Sarah Perez","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tech-antitrust-hearing-banner.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn84@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596115814639_b509d3f7f12e9f30.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn92@2020_6/2020-07-30/1596115814221_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn72@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115829689_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn48@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115828238_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=XlpdmL_I7xo:ABONlZk9tJQ:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn100@2020_1/2020-07-30/1596115829248_4e02bbaff547dbf1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=XlpdmL_I7xo:ABONlZk9tJQ:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn16@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596115829283_b5afe72aae7be30e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn92@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115830290_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/XlpdmL_I7xo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn52@2020_2/2020-07-30/1596115830043_48c6b372ec48bc71.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 21:30:10","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 13:30:10","title":"In antitrust hearing, Zuckerberg admits Facebook has copied its competition","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024146","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">At the House Antitrust Subcommittee hearings this afternoon, <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/facebook\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"facebook\">Facebook <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> CEO Mark Zuckerberg was directly questioned about his company&#8217;s strategy of copying competitors&#8217; app and features, and even threatening to do so as a negotiation tactic amid M&#38;A discussions. In his response, Zuckerberg was forced to admit the obvious: that Facebook, he said, has &#8220;certainly adapted features that others have led in.&#8221;</p>\n<p>However, he denied any characterization claiming Facebook used such tactics in an anti-competitive way &#8212; for example, to pressure a company to sell to Facebook instead of trying to compete with it.</p>\n<p>In one particular line of questioning between Rep. Pramila Jayapal (D-WA) and Facebook&#8217;s CEO, she asked specifically about the company&#8217;s billion-dollar <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2012/04/09/facebook-to-acquire-instagram-for-1-billion/\">acquisition of Instagram in 2012</a>. The M&#38;A deal had been <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/29/facebook-instagram-deal-illegal-nadler/\">already been brought up repeatedly</a> throughout the hearing as an example of Facebook buying its way into expanded market power.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Jayapal led into the questions around <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/instagram\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"instagram\">Instagram <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> by first painting a picture of a company where execs agreed that copying from other apps was a viable business strategy.</p>\n<p>She specifically referenced <a href=\"https://judiciary.house.gov/uploadedfiles/0005351500053516.pdf\">emails from 2012</a> between Zuckerberg and Facebook COO Sheryl Sandberg where the CEO had written that by moving faster, Facebook could &#8220;prevent our competitors from getting footholds.&#8221; Sandberg had responded that &#8220;it is hard not to agree it that is better to do more and move faster, especially if that means you don&#8217;t have competitors build products that takes some of our users.&#8221; A PM had also chimed in that they would love to see Facebook being &#8220;even more aggressive and nimble&#8221; in copying competitors, Jayapal noted.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2024043\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024043\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2024043\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"Mark Zuckerberg\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg 1920w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024043\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> TechCrunch/screenshot</p></div></p>\n<p>The emails had hinted at the birth of Facebook&#8217;s strategy around copying its competition, as they detailed meetings between a high-level Facebook employee and the Renren founders as well as Robin Li from China&#8217;s Baidu.</p>\n<p>The employee had learned of the overall culture of cloning products quickly in the Chinese app market.  Renren had built its own version of Pinterest and Tumblr, the emails said, as well as games, a music product and more. And Tencent QQ had then just released a messaging app similar to the walkie-talkie app Voxer in the U.S. It was pointed out that maybe it was easier to move quickly because these companies were &#8220;just copying other people,&#8221; the email suggested.</p>\n<p>Zuckerberg had forwarded the email to Sandberg, noting &#8220;you&#8217;ll probably find this interesting and agree.&#8221; And she did.</p>\n<p>Under questioning, Zuckerberg declined to say how many companies Facebook had copied since the 2012 email exchange, bristling that he didn&#8217;t agree with the premise of the question.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Our job is to make sure that we build the best services for people to connect with all the people they care about. And a lot of that is done by innovating and by building new things&#8230;,&#8221; he began, before being cut off.</p>\n<p>Jayapal then asked if Facebook had ever threatened to clone a product from another company while attempting to acquire it.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Not that I recall,&#8221; Zuckerberg said.</p>\n<p>However, it seems Facebook had threatened to use <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2012/05/24/facebook-camera/\">its &#8220;Facebook Camera&#8221; app</a> against Instagram ahead of the latter&#8217;s acquisition, Jayapal noted. In a chat with Instagram co-founder Kevin Systrom, Zuckerberg said Facebook was developing its own photo strategy, and how we engage now will also determine how much we&#8217;re partners versus competitors down the line, she explained. <a href=\"https://www.scribd.com/document/470826155/House-Judiciary-Facebook-text-log-between-Mark-Zuckerberg-and-Kevin-Systrom\">In an email chain</a>, Zuckerberg had told Systrom that &#8220;at some point, you&#8217;ll need to figure out how you actually want to work with us.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The Instagram founder had also <a href=\"https://www.scribd.com/document/470826365/House-Judiciary-Chat-log-between-Kevin-Systrom-and-Matt-Cohler\">confided in an investor</a> that he felt Zuckerberg&#8217;s comments were a threat, Jayapal said, and was concerned that Facebook would go into &#8220;destroy mode&#8221; if he didn&#8217;t sell Instagram.</p>\n<p>Zuckerberg didn&#8217;t deny the conversation, but disagreed again with the characterization, saying it was clear that this was a space the two companies would compete in.</p>\n<p>Jayapal asked also if a similar tactic was used against Snapchat in its attempts to acquire the company.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I don&#8217;t remember those specific conversations,&#8221; Zuckerberg responded. &#8220;But that was also an area where was very clear that we were going to be building something,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>Jayapal concluded her time by stating that she did believe Facebook was a monopoly because of this and other behavior.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I think the question again here is when the dominant platform threatens as potential rivals, that should not be a normal business practice. Facebook is a case study, in my opinion, in monopoly power because your company harvests and monetizes our data, and then your company uses that data to spy on competitors, and to copy acquire and kill rivals,&#8221; she said.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/tech-antitrust-hearing\"><img src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tech-antitrust-hearing-banner.jpg\" /></a></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Sy1LV79Vu3w:-dRkOfV029I:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img 21:32:05 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?w=680","linkMd5":"901f09a5cd85eae9d76a075ae0dd7edc","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn80@2020_1/2020-07-30/1596115814650_734b0f310905069a.webp","author":"Sarah Perez","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/zuckerberg-testimony.jpg?w=680":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn80@2020_1/2020-07-30/1596115814650_734b0f310905069a.webp","https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/tech-antitrust-hearing-banner.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn84@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596115814639_b509d3f7f12e9f30.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn92@2020_6/2020-07-30/1596115814221_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn72@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115829689_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn48@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115828238_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Sy1LV79Vu3w:-dRkOfV029I:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn36@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596115828175_654760db83c585f7.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Sy1LV79Vu3w:-dRkOfV029I:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn28@2020_6/2020-07-30/1596115828259_3397134d7fbe854c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn92@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115830290_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/Sy1LV79Vu3w":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn64@2020_5/2020-07-30/1596115829146_c86d4bd79c5cb336.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 21:30:10","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 13:30:10","title":"Panasonic boosts energy density, trims cobalt in new 2170 battery cell for Tesla","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024312","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/panasonic\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"panasonic\">Panasonic <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> has developed new battery technology for the &#8216;2170&#8217; lithium-ion cells it produces and supplies to Tesla, a change that improves energy density by 5% and reduces costly cobalt content.</p>\n<p>The new, higher-energy dense 2170 cells will be produced by Panasonic at <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/tesla-motors\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"tesla-motors\">Tesla&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> factory in Sparks, Nevada, the company said Thursday. Panasonic is upgrading its battery cell lines with production slated to begin in September. The company operates 13 lines at the factory with a capacity to produce 35 gigawatt hours of batteries each year. All 13 lines will eventually run the new technology, Panasonic Energy North America President Allan Swan said without providing a timeline of when the entire system would be upgraded.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;re about to take another leap forward,&#8221; Swan said in a recent interview. &#8220;It&#8217;s kind of exciting from the Panasonic perspective; we&#8217;re driving towards cobalt free and we&#8217;re driving towards higher energy dense batteries, which gives our customers a choice of how they want utilize that.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The facility where these new battery cells will be produced is known as Gigafactory 1, <span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">a critical component of Tesla&#8217;s plan to expand global battery capacity and reduce the cost of electric vehicles. Panasonic has been its most important partner in that project, which based <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/ix?doc=/Archives/edgar/data/1318605/000156459020029536/tsla-8k_20200610.htm\">on a recent agreement</a> should last until at least 2023. </span>Panasonic makes the 2170 cells at Gigafactory 1, which Tesla then uses to make battery packs for the Model 3. The 2170 cells are also used in Tesla&#8217;s newest vehicle, the Model Y.</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s a quick primer. A battery contains two electrodes. There’s an anode (negative) on one side and a cathode (positive) on the other. An electrolyte sits in the middle and acts as the courier that moves ions between the electrodes when charging and discharging.</p>\n<p>A cell with greater energy density means that engineers figured out a way to pack more energy in that space. The 5% improvement in energy density in the cells should result in the same gains in Tesla&#8217;s battery packs. The upshot: Tesla&#8217;s Model 3 and Model Y could see improvements in range. The reduction in cobalt content, a rare chemical element that is expensive and has social and environmental costs, could also help reduce the price of the cells.</p>\n<p>Panasonic&#8217;s factories in Japan produce the cylindrical lithium-ion “18650” cells, which are used to power Tesla’s Model S and Model X vehicles. Panasonic has already improved 18650 cells, resulting in a reduction in cobalt and improvement in energy density.</p>\n<p>Panasonic uses a NCA, or nickel-cobalt-aluminium, cathode chemistry in its battery cells. Panasonic wouldn&#8217;t disclose the amount of cobalt used today or get into the details of its technology. However, Celina Mikolajczak, vice president of battery technology at Panasonic Energy of North America, did say that the total amount of cobalt used in Panasonic cylindrical automotive batteries is less than 2% of global demand.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Mikolajczak said that </span>NCA uses less cobalt than NCM, or nickel manganese cobalt oxide. The NCA cathode chemistry has been further developed to reduce cobalt, she added<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">. </span></p>\n<p>The company is aiming for zero cobalt in its battery cells, Mikolajczak said. Panasonic has already managed that feat in its R&#38;D lab. The<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> plan is to commercialize cobalt-free batteries in a few years.</span></p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 21:30:10","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 13:30:10","title":"Amazon’s hardware business doesn’t escape Congressional scrutiny","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024313","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">While much of today&#8217;s <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/29/big-tech-cicilline-pandemic-antitrust-hearing/\">Congressional grilling into the anticompetitive practices of the big tech giants</a> focused on their core businesses, Amazon&#8217;s hardware also came in for close inspection during the hours-long interrogation.</p>\n<p>It was a small but significant exchange, because it touched on the breadth of the company&#8217;s services and how dominance in one area can mean potentially anti-competitive behavior in another part of the tech giant&#8217;s business.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"TskXjdQr1o\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/29/big-tech-cicilline-pandemic-antitrust-hearing/\">Lawmakers argue that big tech stands to benefit from the pandemic and must be regulated</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Lawmakers argue that big tech stands to benefit from the pandemic and must be regulated&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/29/big-tech-cicilline-pandemic-antitrust-hearing/embed/#?secret=TskXjdQr1o\" data-secret=\"TskXjdQr1o\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>For Maryland&#8217;s Representative Jamie Raskin, both Amazon&#8217;s best-selling <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B07R1CXKN7?tag=mh0b-20&#38;hvadid=78271518759182&#38;hvqmt=e&#38;hvbmt=be&#38;hvdev=c&#38;ref=pd_sl_2g7cb1h5zl_e\">Echo</a> and the <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/b/?ie=UTF8&#38;node=8521791011&#38;tag=mh0b-20&#38;hvadid=78615109214187&#38;hvqmt=e&#38;hvbmt=be&#38;hvdev=c&#38;ref=pd_sl_18xa831llk_e\">Fire TV devices</a> became targets thanks to recent reporting on the company&#8217;s business practices and negotiations regarding both devices.</p>\n<p>The Echo is the company&#8217;s foray into the smart home market that&#8217;s widely seen as the next major battleground in consumer technology. It&#8217;s one of the most widely adopted pieces of Amazon&#8217;s technology and has captured about 60% of the smart home market, according to Raskin.</p>\n<p>The congressman hammered Bezos on two points about the Echo. The first was the company&#8217;s pricing scheme which had the Echo priced well below the cost to produce the device making it all but impossible for other tech companies to compete.</p>\n<p>The Echo&#8217;s wide adoption has also led Amazon to engage in other anti-competitive behavior, Raskin asserted — some of which was outlined in previous questioning from Colorado Rep. Ken Buck <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/amazon-tech-startup-echo-bezos-alexa-investment-fund-11595520249\">citing a Wall Street Journal report</a> that Amazon had used its investment unit focused on its Echo product and Alexa voice assistant to copy technology coming from small startup companies.</p>\n<p>But beyond its appropriation of another company&#8217;s intellectual property, Amazon also used the Echo platform to promote its own products over competitors when customers used its voice services.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Is Alexa trained to favor Amazon products?&#8221; Raskin asked.</p>\n<p>Bezos responded that he wasn&#8217;t sure if Amazon had specifically trained the Alexa to default to Amazon services or to promote the company&#8217;s own brand of products, but that he wouldn&#8217;t be surprised. &#8220;It wouldn&#8217;t surprise me if Alexa sometimes does promote our own products,&#8221; the Amazon chief executive said.</p>\n<p>Raskin also took Bezos to task for the company&#8217;s recent negotiations with WarnerMedia, the production studio, streaming service, and network giant. Specifically, he was concerned with how negotiations around the distribution of WarnerMedia&#8217;s HBO Max service on the company&#8217;s Fire TV devices included discussions around Amazon&#8217;s access to WarnerMedia productions.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;You’re not only asking for financial terms but also for content from Warner Media,&#8221; Raskin said. &#8220;Is it fair to use your gatekeeper status role in the streaming device market to promote your position as a competitor in the video streaming market with respect to content?&#8221;</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Bezos responded that the negotiations were &#8220;normal commerce,&#8221; but Raskin tried to make the case that the negotiations over access to the Fire was yet another way in which the company&#8217;s leverage in one market impacted its ability to exercise unfair advantage against a competitor in a different industry. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">&#8220;</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You’re using your control over access to people’s living rooms essentially,&#8221; Raskin said. &#8220;You’re using that to obtain leverage in terms of getting creative content that you want. Are you essentially converting power in one domain into power in another domain where it doesn’t belong?&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>The comments and line of inquiry from Raskin were part of an intense bout of questioning that seemed to hone in on the purported topic of the hearings — the anti-competitive and potentially monopolistic power wielded by four of the nation&#8217;s largest tech companies. Facebook, Apple and Alphabet were all raked over the Congressional coals in bouts of questioning, but it seemed that the most sustained criticism on anti-competitive behavior was reserved for Bezos and Amazon.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"5KhJGyDRBc\"><p><a Shieber","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn92@2020_6/2020-07-30/1596115814221_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn72@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115829689_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn48@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115828238_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=vGS0vCPpYzI:czzlgW3zFKo:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn68@2020_2/2020-07-30/1596115829203_47592c787e182525.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=vGS0vCPpYzI:czzlgW3zFKo:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn84@2020_1/2020-07-30/1596115828218_08882b70e3adac40.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn92@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115830290_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/vGS0vCPpYzI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn24@2020_6/2020-07-30/1596115828193_92bac8078a5fb78f.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 21:30:10","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 13:30:10","title":"New Relic is changing its pricing model to encourage broader monitoring","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024933","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">In the monitoring world, typically when you spin up a new instance, you pay a fee to monitor it. If you are particularly active in any given month, that can result in a hefty bill at the end of the month. That leads to limiting what you choose to monitor to control costs. <a href=\"https://newrelic.com/\">New Relic</a> wants to change that, and today it announced that it&#8217;s moving to a model where customers pay by the user instead with a smaller less costly data component.</p>\n<p>The company is also simplifying its product set with the goal of encouraging customers to instrument everything instead of deciding what to monitor and what to leave out to control cost. &#8220;What we&#8217;re announcing is a completely reimagined platform. We&#8217;re simplifying our products from 11 to three, and we eliminate those barriers to standardizing on a single source of truth,&#8221; <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/new-relic\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"new-relic\">New Relic <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> founder and CEO Lew Cirne told TechCrunch.</p>\n<p>The way the company can afford to make this switch is by exposing the underlying telemetry database that it created to run its own products. By taking advantage of this database to track all of your APM, tracing and metric data all in one place, Cirne says they can control costs much better and pass those savings onto customers, whose bills should be much smaller based on a this new pricing model, he said.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;Prior to this, there has not been any technology that&#8217;s good at gathering all of those data types into a single database, what we would call a telemetry database. And we actually created one ourselves and it&#8217;s the backbone of all of our products. [Up until now], we haven&#8217;t really exposed it to our customers, so that they can put all their data into it,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2024937\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2024937\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2024937\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Telemetry-Data-Platform-Metrics.png?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"383\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Telemetry-Data-Platform-Metrics.png 3840w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Telemetry-Data-Platform-Metrics.png?resize=150,84 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Telemetry-Data-Platform-Metrics.png?resize=300,169 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Telemetry-Data-Platform-Metrics.png?resize=768,432 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Telemetry-Data-Platform-Metrics.png?resize=680,383 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Telemetry-Data-Platform-Metrics.png?resize=1536,864 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Telemetry-Data-Platform-Metrics.png?resize=2048,1152 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/Telemetry-Data-Platform-Metrics.png?resize=50,28 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2024937\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">New Relic Telemetry Data. Image<b>: </b>New Relic</p></div></p>\n<p>The company is distilling the product set into three main categories. The first is the Telemetry Data Platform, which offers a single way to gather any events, logs or traces, whether from their agents or someone else&#8217;s or even open source monitoring tools like Prometheus.</p>\n<p>The second product is called Full-stack Observability. This includes all of their previous products, which were sold separately such as APM, mobility, infrastructure and logging. Finally they are offering an intelligence layer called New Relic AI.</p>\n<p>Cirne says by simplifying the product set and changing the way they bill, it will save customers money through the efficiencies they have uncovered. In practice he says, pricing will consist of a combination of users and data, but he believes their approach will result in much lower bills and more cost certainty for customers.</p>\n<p>&#8220;It&#8217;ll vary by customer so this is just a rough estimate but imagine that the typical New Relic bill under this model will be a 70% per user charge and 30% data charge, roughly, but so if that&#8217;s the case, and if you look at our competitors, 100% of the bill is data,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p>The new approach is available starting today. Companies can try it with 100 GB single user account.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=B2KMBmtmI7k:MAeKLcQTEzc:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img 21:30:10","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 13:30:10","title":"Samsung’s second-quarter profit grew 23% year-over-year, thanks to strong chip demand","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024879","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https://www.samsung.com/us/aboutsamsung/home/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Samsung Electronics</a> sounded a cautiously optimistic note in its <a href=\"https://images.samsung.com/is/content/samsung/p5/global/ir/docs/2020_2Q_conference_eng.pdf\">earnings report today</a>. The company is continuing to deal with the fallout of the COVID-19 pandemic, but its memory business was fortified by demand for DRAM chips as data centers adapted to an increase in remote work and education.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/samsung-electronics\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"samsung-electronics\">Samsung Electronics <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> will launch new models of its flagship smartphones, including the Galaxy Note and a foldable device, at its online Galaxy Unpacked event on August 5, but will also focus on increasing sales of low- to mid-priced phones, which it expects to drive revenue during the rest of the year.</p>\n<p>Second-quarter operating profit grew 26% from the previous quarter, and 23% year-over-year to 8.15 trillion won (about $6.84 billion), due largely to more sales of DRAM chips. Revenue fell 4% from the previous quarter, and 6% year-over-year, to 53 trillion won, while net profit rose 7% to 5.6 trillion won. Samsung said revenue was impacted by lower sales of smartphones and other devices, but some of that was offset by reduced marketing spending and other cost-cutting measures.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Rr0b3GEI7H\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/07/samsung-will-reveal-the-next-galaxy-note-on-august-5/\">Samsung will reveal the next Galaxy Note on August 5</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Samsung will reveal the next Galaxy Note on August 5&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/07/samsung-will-reveal-the-next-galaxy-note-on-august-5/embed/#?secret=Rr0b3GEI7H\" data-secret=\"Rr0b3GEI7H\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The company also acknowledged that it faces intense competition from other smartphone makers. In fact, on the same day that Samsung announced its second-quarter earnings, research firm Canalys <a href=\"https://www.canalys.com/newsroom/Canalys-huawei-samsung-worldwide-smartphone-market-q2-2020?ctid=1556-1195484408fbbb34e0298b96eddb178f\">released a report </a>that said Huawei shipped more smartphones globally than any other vendor in the second-quarter, despite dealing with American government restrictions, displacing Samsung from the top position for the first time.</p>\n<p>On the brighter side, many analysts believe that Samsung, along with TSMC, will benefit from Intel’s recent announcement that<a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/article/us-samsung-elec-intel-stocks/samsung-electronics-shares-rally-on-intels-chip-outsourcing-plan-idUSKCN24T0C5\"> it will outsource more semiconductor manufacturing</a>.</p>\n<h3>Remote services drove demand for DRAM chips</h3>\n<p>The company’s semiconductor division was helped by demand for DRAM chips from data centers that need to fortify their online infrastructure to support remote workers and online education. PC demand also remained solid because of low-end laptop sales.</p>\n<p>But sales of chips for mobile devices remained weak as consumers spent less money because of the pandemic. When they did make purchases, they tended to buy low- to mid-end mobile products, which use less powerful chips.</p>\n<h3>A “one-off gain” boosted display revenue</h3>\n<p>Samsung Electronic’s display panel business earnings improved quarter-over-quarter thanks to a “one-off gain” that boosted profits from mobile displays. Samsung did not give details about where the gain came form, but Bloomberg <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2020-07-29/samsung-beats-estimates-on-recovery-of-chips-and-gadget-sales\">reports</a> it was a compensatory payment of about 1.1 trillion won ($924 million) from Apple after the iPhone maker ordered fewer displays than expected.</p>\n<p>But overall demand for displays was lower as COVID-19 hit smartphone sales. Operating losses were offset slightly by purchases of monitors by people working from home.</p>\n<p>Samsung Electronics said mobile display demand is expected to recover this year as its biggest clients continue to launch new products, despite continuing uncertainties from the pandemic. It also expects orders for mobile and graphic chips to increase as new smartphones and game consoles are released, and anticipates a &#8220;full-fledged rebound in earnings from mobile displays&#8221; by the end of the year, due largely to sales of mid- to low-end smartphones.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a 2022","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024913","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Japanese new space startup ispace has revealed the final design of its HAKUTO-R lunar lander, a spacecraft set to make its first touchdown on the Moon in 2022 if all goes to the updated plan (it had been set to fly in October 2021 until today). ispace is part of a team led by Draper selected by NASA for its Commercial Lunar Payload Services (CLPS) program to deliver various payloads to the Moon ahead of NASA planned human mission to the lunar surface in 2024.</p>\n<p>The lander is just a bit taller than a person, at around seven and a half feet tall (it&#8217;s basically that wide and long as well). The design includes a 4K color camera that will beam back images throughout the mission, as well as fuel tanks for holding its propellant, solar panels for power generation, landing gear, thrusters and payload compartments for holding up to 66 lbs of experiments and other materials.</p>\n<p><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/rzriat-Ex18?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>ispace also announced adjusted timing for its first lunar lander missions for HAKUTO-R as mentioned. The first will now take place in 2022, using a SpaceX Falcon 9 rocket, and carrying commercial payloads including equipment for conducting scientific experiments. The second is now set for 2023, and will carry a small rover that will survey the Moon and pave the way for potential long-term commercial investment on the lunar surface.</p>\n<p>[gallery Etherington","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn92@2020_6/2020-07-30/1596115814221_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn72@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115829689_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn48@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115828238_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=EMJTyRs3Oo8:9ndneRBta0Y:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn60@2020_5/2020-07-30/1596115828227_26d65d9faeec5518.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=EMJTyRs3Oo8:9ndneRBta0Y:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn76@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596115828257_4339148c825080f0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn92@2020_4/2020-07-30/1596115830290_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/EMJTyRs3Oo8":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn88@2020_3/2020-07-30/1596115830004_a48aa94b5bfcaa2b.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 21:30:10","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 13:30:10","title":"NASA successfully launches its Mars 2020 Perseverance rover using an Atlas V rocket","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2024914","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">NASA has launched one of its most crucial science missions to date, the <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/mars\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"mars\">Mars <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> 2020 mission that carries its Perseverance robotic rover. This rover, a successor to the Curiosity robotic explorer, is equipped with sensors specifically designed to help it hopefully fund evidence of ancient, microbiotic life on Mars.</p>\n<p>Mars 2020 departed from Cape Canaveral in Florida at 7:50 AM EDT (4:50 PM PDT). Perseverance was loaded atop a United Launch Alliance (ULA) Atlas V rocket, which had a good liftoff and deployed its second stage which put the spacecraft into a parking orbit as it readies to depart on its trip towards Mars, which will see it arrive in February 2021.</p>\n<p>Once at Mars, the lander vehicle will take Perseverance down to the planet&#8217;s surface on February 18, 2021, to a target landing zone found in what&#8217;s known as Jezero Crater. This location on Mars was once a lake, long ago when the atmosphere on Mars was quite different than the dry, dusty and cold environment we know today. This has been chosen specifically because it&#8217;s a prime spot for finding any evidence of microbiological life that might exist, since it contains one of the best-preserved deposits of a river delta on Mars.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>NASA scientists don&#8217;t expect to be able to confirm the existence of life on Mars using the instruments on Perseverance, however – they think they can find strong indications that the conditions and materials necessary for life once existed, but the ultimate proof could come from the ambitious Mars sample return mission being planned for 2026. This would involve NASA launching a return rocket to the red planet, which will carry a rocket that can take off from the Mars surface with samples collected by Perseverance on board. That would then meet up with a rover to be launched by the European Space Agency (<a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/esa\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"esa\">ESA) <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> which would then make the trip all the way back to Earth for scientists to study.</p>\n<p>In addition to its contained, radioactive nuclear battery power source, environment sensors, cameras and a suite of other instruments to help pick up any preserved evidence of ancient life, Perseverance is equipped with microphones. This is the first time that microphones are making the trip to the surface of another world, and it means we could hear what it sounds like on the surface of another world, something we&#8217;ve never done before.</p>\n<p>Perseverance also carries the Mars Ingenuity helicopter, a small drone designed for first-ever self-powered flight, which is also designed to warm itself to survive the cold Martian night. It is set to hopefully make up to five flights in 30 days, could include color photos – the first ever taken from an aerial vantage point.</p>\n<p>This is a great first step for this historic Mars 2020 mission, and now we&#8217;ll wait and watch for other significant milestones, including next in around two weeks when the spacecraft fires its engines for its departure from Earth&#8217;s orbit and begins the long trip to Mars.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=gExUMqZZ57A:3B7rSYG16Xg:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/21X5lGlDOfg?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;fs=1&#038;autohide=2&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;'></iframe></p>\n<p>NASA is set to launch its newest rover to <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/mars\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"mars\">Mars <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> later this morning. The liftoff is set for 7:50 AM EDT (4:50 AM PDT), with a broadcast beginning at 7:00 AM EDT (4:00 AM PDT). This mission will launch a ULA Atlas V rocket to carry the Perseverance rover to Mars with a trip that will last several months, arriving in February 2021.</p>\n<p>The 2,260-lb rover is equipped with a range of sensors to help it search for signs of past micro organic life on Mars, as well as study the planet&#8217;s amtospheric and geological makeup. It also carries with it a helicopter drone called Ingenuity, which will seek to become the first ever vehicle to take-off and fly within the Mars atmosphere.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Perseverance is a big upgrade over prior rovers in a number of ways. It can cover way more ground operating autonomously per day than any of its predecessors, for instance, which should help it conduct more science than ever before. It&#8217;s also equipped with 19 cameras to provide a full, detailed and high-quality view of its surroundings back to Earth. The rover is also designed to prime the pump for future human Mars exploration (and long-duration human Moon missions), with experiments on board like MOXIE, an instrument that will create oxygen from the CO2 found in Mars&#8217; atmosphere, and will set the stage for a washing machine-sized version to be developed in future that will essentially act as a self-sustaining Mars power source.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_1955125\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-1955125\" class=\"size-full wp-image-1955125\" The plan is to ultimately combine the efforts of NASA and the European Space Agency to retrieve samples of Martian soil that Perseverance leaves behind in collection canisters using a future spacecraft and retrieval lander, so that they can be studied directly back here on Earth.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a
